[2025-12-01T08:50:05Z] Kartikey Pradhan: Q. There’s no single agreed-upon origin for Y, but one theory traces it to the 14th century. Latin writers began shortening the word for “weight” and drew a bar to show that letters were connected. As handwriting sped up, the letters and the bar gradually merged, eventually forming how we know it today. An AT&T employee felt it deserved an official name, and called it Y, a portmanteau combining a word referring to the number of points in it and the surname of his favourite football player, Jim. Identify Y.

[2025-12-01T09:59:29Z] Pavan Pamidimarri: This English word X comes to us from the name of a Roman office of magistrate. The Roman office itself was named after a Latin word that means “to assess.” This Roman magistrate was responsible for assessing and registering citizens and their property and supervising public morals. X took on its current meaning in recent centuries. From the name of the same office, we get another English word Y which is closer to its original meaning, and it is used mostly by governments for official purposes. ID X and Y.
